The tower notifies FSS of your departure, and FSS passes your ETA to your destination. About halfway to your destination, you encounter a severe cold front with extensive thundersorm development and decide to cancel your IFR clearance and land at a nearby civilian field to wait out the storm. Upon landing you forget to call FSS to close out your flight plan. Thirty minutes after your ETA, FSS calls the destination to see if you arrived.  Since you haven’t, their next step is to contact Approach Control to see if you are under their control. Approach has not heard from you so ARTCC is contacted, and they say you canceled your IFR clearance but gave no further intentions.  The local FSS has no record of a VFR flight plan, and you don’t answer any radio calls.   Since there is no record of your landing, there is a strong possibility that you may have crashed, and a SAR effort is launched.   Situations as described above could have been avoided by contacting FSS after landing.  As OPNAVINST 3710.7 states, you are responsible for doing this or having it done.  At a military field, a call to Ground Control is sufficient as you clear the duty.  At a civilian field, a phone call or personal visit is required.  Failure to do so may result in a flight violation.
